       <b>
        Dunedin
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">
            ʌ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-nz-Dunedin.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/En-nz-Dunedin.ogg" title="En-nz-Dunedin.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         duh-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          NEE
         </span>
         -din
        </i>
       </a>
       ) (
       <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">
        Māori
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="mi" xml:lang="mi">
         <b>
          Ōtepoti
         </b>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is the second-largest city in the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">
        South Island
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">
        New Zealand
       </a>
       , and the principal city of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago" title="Otago">
        Otago
       </a>
       region. Its name comes from
       <i>
        Dùn Èideann
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">
        Scottish Gaelic
       </a>
       name for
       <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">
        Edinburgh
       </a>
       , the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
        Scotland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The urban area lies on the central-eastern coast of Otago, surrounding the head of
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       . The harbour and hills around Dunedin represent the remnants of an extinct volcano. The city suburbs extend out into the surrounding valleys and hills, onto the isthmus of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       , and along the shores of the Otago Harbour and the Pacific Ocean. Dunedin was the largest New Zealand city by territorial land area until superseded by Auckland on the creation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Council" title="Auckland Council">
        Auckland Council
       </a>
       in November 2010.
      </p>
      <p>
       Archaeological evidence points to the area having been long inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="Māori people">
        Māori
       </a>
       prior to the European arrival. The province of Otago takes its name from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ngai_Tahu" title="Ngai Tahu">
        Ngai Tahu
       </a>
       village of
       <a href="/wiki/Otakou" title="Otakou">
        Otakou
       </a>
       at the mouth of the harbour,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       that became a whaling station in the 1830s.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1848 a Scottish settlement was established by the Lay Association of the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_Scotland_(1843%E2%80%931900)" title="Free Church of Scotland (1843–1900)">
        Free Church of Scotland
       </a>
       . Between 1855 and 1900 many thousands of
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_New_Zealanders" title="Scottish New Zealanders">
        Scots
       </a>
       emigrated to the incorporated city. Dunedin became wealthy during the central
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Gold_Rush" title="Otago Gold Rush">
        Otago Gold Rush
       </a>
       , beginning in the 1860s. In the mid-1860s, and between 1878 and 1881, it was New Zealand's largest urban area. The city population at 5 March 2013 was 120,246.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While
       <a href="/wiki/Tauranga" title="Tauranga">
        Tauranga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Napier-Hastings_Urban_Area" title="Napier-Hastings Urban Area">
        Napier-Hastings
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_New_Zealand" title="Hamilton, New Zealand">
        Hamilton
       </a>
       have eclipsed the city in size of population since the 1980s to make it only the seventh-largest urban area in New Zealand, Dunedin is still considered one of the four main
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities_of_New_Zealand" title="Cities of New Zealand">
        cities of New Zealand
       </a>
       for historic, cultural and geographic reasons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin has a diverse economy, which includes manufacturing, publishing and technology-based industries as well as education, research and tourism. The city's most important activity centres around
       <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education_in_New_Zealand" title="Tertiary education in New Zealand">
        tertiary education
       </a>
       – Dunedin is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago" title="University of Otago">
        University of Otago
       </a>
       , New Zealand's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_New_Zealand" title="List of universities in New Zealand">
        oldest university
       </a>
       (established 1869), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Polytechnic" title="Otago Polytechnic">
        Otago Polytechnic
       </a>
       . Students account for a large proportion of the population; 21.6 percent of the city's population was aged between 15 and 24 at the 2006 census, compared to the New Zealand average of 14.2 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2014 Dunedin was designated as a UNESCO
       <a href="/wiki/City_of_Literature" title="City of Literature">
        City of Literature
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dunedin" title="History of Dunedin">
        History of Dunedin
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span id="M.C4.81ori_settlements">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Māori_settlements">
        Māori settlements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Māori settlements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Archaeological evidence shows the first human (Māori) occupation of New Zealand occurred between AD 1250–1300,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-settled_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-settled-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with population concentrated along the southeast coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamel2001_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamel2001-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndersonAllinghamSmith1996_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndersonAllinghamSmith1996-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A camp site at Kaikai Beach, near
       <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_New_Zealand" title="Long Beach, New Zealand">
        Long Beach
       </a>
       , has been dated from about that time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1983_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1983-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are numerous archaic (
       <a href="/wiki/Moa" title="Moa">
        moa
       </a>
       hunter) sites in what is now Dunedin, several of them large and permanently occupied, particularly in the 14th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndersonAllinghamSmith1996_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndersonAllinghamSmith1996-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamel2001_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamel2001-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The population contracted but expanded again with the evolution of the Classic culture which saw the building of several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C4%81_(M%C4%81ori)" title="Pā (Māori)">
        pā
       </a>
       , fortified settlements, notably Pukekura at (
       <a href="/wiki/Taiaroa_Head" title="Taiaroa Head">
        Taiaroa Head
       </a>
       ), about 1650.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was a settlement in what is now central Dunedin (Ōtepoti) occupied as late as about 1785 but abandoned by 1826.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle2005_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle2005-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Maori tradition tells first of a people called Kahui Tipua living in the area, then Te Rapuwai, semi-legendary but considered to be historical. The next arrivals were
       <a href="/wiki/Waitaha" title="Waitaha">
        Waitaha
       </a>
       followed by
       <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81ti_Mamoe" title="Kāti Mamoe">
        Kāti Mamoe
       </a>
       late in the 16th century and then
       <a href="/wiki/Ng%C4%81i_Tahu" title="Ngāi Tahu">
        Kai Tahu
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Ngai Tahu
       </i>
       in modern standard
       <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">
        Māori
       </a>
       ) who arrived in the mid 17th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These migration waves have often been represented as 'invasions' in European accounts but modern scholarship has cast doubt on that. They were probably migrations like those of the European which incidentally resulted in bloodshed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1983_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1983-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998_22-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1998-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The sealer John Boultbee recorded in the 1820s that the 'Kaika Otargo' (settlements around and near
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       ) were the oldest and largest in the south.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeggBegg1979_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeggBegg1979-27">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_settlement">
        European settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Lieutenant
       <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">
        James Cook
       </a>
       stood off what is now the coast of Dunedin between 25 February 1770 and 5 March 1770, naming
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Saunders" title="Cape Saunders">
        Cape Saunders
       </a>
       (on the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       ) and Saddle Hill. He reported penguins and seals in the vicinity, which led
       <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">
        sealers
       </a>
       to visit from the beginning of the 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeaglehole1955–67_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeaglehole1955–67-28">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The early years of sealing saw a feud between sealers and local Maori from 1810 to 1823, the "
       <a href="/wiki/Sealers%27_War" title="Sealers' War">
        Sealers' War
       </a>
       " sparked by an incident on Otago Harbour, but
       <a href="/wiki/William_Tucker_(settler)" title="William Tucker (settler)">
        William Tucker
       </a>
       became the first European to settle in the area in 1815.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle2005_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle2005-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Permanent European occupation dates from 1831, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Weller_brothers" title="Weller brothers">
        Weller brothers
       </a>
       founded their whaling station at Otago, modern
       <a href="/wiki/Otakou" title="Otakou">
        Otakou
       </a>
       , on the Otago Harbour. Epidemics badly reduced the Maori population. By the late 1830s the Harbour had become an international whaling port.
       <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Jones_(pioneer)" title="Johnny Jones (pioneer)">
        Johnny Jones
       </a>
       established a farming settlement and a mission station, the South Island's first, at
       <a href="/wiki/Waikouaiti" title="Waikouaiti">
        Waikouaiti
       </a>
       in 1840.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1998_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1998-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Victoria_statue,_Dunedin,_New_Zealand.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG/170px-Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG/255px-Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG/340px-Queen_Victoria_statue%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Victoria_statue,_Dunedin,_New_Zealand.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Statue of
         <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">
          Queen Victoria
         </a>
         , at Queens Gardens. Dunedin was settled by Europeans during the
         <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">
          Victorian era
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1844, the
       <i>
        Deborah
       </i>
       , captained by Thomas Wing and carrying (among others) his wife Lucy and a representative of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Company" title="New Zealand Company">
        New Zealand Company
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Tuckett" title="Frederick Tuckett">
        Frederick Tuckett
       </a>
       , sailed south to determine the location of a planned
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_Scotland_(1843%E2%80%931900)" title="Free Church of Scotland (1843–1900)">
        Free Church
       </a>
       settlement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After inspecting several areas around the eastern coast of the south island, Tuckett selected the site which would become known as Dunedin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Tuckett turned down the site which would become
       <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
        Christchurch
       </a>
       , as he felt the ground around the
       <a href="/wiki/Avon_River_(Canterbury)" title="Avon River (Canterbury)">
        Avon river
       </a>
       was swampy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cargill%27s_Monument,_Dunedin,_NZ.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG/170px-Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG/255px-Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG/340px-Cargill%27s_Monument%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cargill%27s_Monument,_Dunedin,_NZ.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Monument to
         <a href="/wiki/William_Cargill" title="William Cargill">
          William Cargill
         </a>
         on
         <a href="/wiki/Princes_Street,_Dunedin" title="Princes Street, Dunedin">
          Princes Street
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Lay Association of the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_Scotland_(1843%E2%80%931900)" title="Free Church of Scotland (1843–1900)">
        Free Church of Scotland
       </a>
       , through a company called the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Association" title="Otago Association">
        Otago Association
       </a>
       , founded Dunedin at the head of Otago Harbour in 1848 as the principal town of its special settlement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campsie_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campsie-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The name comes from
       <i>
        Dùn Èideann
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">
        Scottish Gaelic
       </a>
       name for
       <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">
        Edinburgh
       </a>
       , the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
        Scotland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kettle" title="Charles Kettle">
        Charles Kettle
       </a>
       the city's surveyor, instructed to emulate the characteristics of Edinburgh, produced a striking, "Romantic" design.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHocken1898_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHocken1898-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There resulted both grand and quirky streets as the builders struggled and sometimes failed to construct his bold vision across the challenging landscape. Captain
       <a href="/wiki/William_Cargill" title="William Cargill">
        William Cargill
       </a>
       , a veteran of the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , served as the secular leader of the new colony. The Reverend
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Burns_(minister)" title="Thomas Burns (minister)">
        Thomas Burns
       </a>
       , a nephew of the poet
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Burns" title="Robert Burns">
        Robert Burns
       </a>
       , provided spiritual guidance. By the end of the 1850s, around 12,000 Scots had emigrated to Dunedin, many from the industrial
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Lowlands" title="Scottish Lowlands">
        lowlands
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campsie_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campsie-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gold_rush_era">
        Gold rush era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Gold rush era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1852, Dunedin became the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Province" title="Otago Province">
        Otago Province
       </a>
       , the whole of New Zealand from the
       <a href="/wiki/Waitaki_River" title="Waitaki River">
        Waitaki
       </a>
       south. In 1861 the discovery of gold at
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel%27s_Gully" title="Gabriel's Gully">
        Gabriel's Gully
       </a>
       , to the southwest, led to a rapid influx of people and saw Dunedin become New Zealand's first city by growth of population in 1865. The new arrivals included many Irish, but also Italians, Lebanese, French, Germans, Jews and Chinese.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949_26-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDonald1965_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDonald1965-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Southern_Cemetery" title="Dunedin Southern Cemetery">
        Dunedin Southern Cemetery
       </a>
       was established in 1858, the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Northern_Cemetery" title="Dunedin Northern Cemetery">
        Dunedin Northern Cemetery
       </a>
       in 1872.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="3615" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg/280px-Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg/420px-Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg/560px-Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Railway_Station_Full_Exterior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_Railway_Station" title="Dunedin Railway Station">
          Dunedin Railway Station
         </a>
         , built in 1906, is famed for its "gingerbread" architecture
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin and the region industrialised and consolidated and the
       <a href="/wiki/Main_South_Line" title="Main South Line">
        Main South Line
       </a>
       connected the city with
       <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
        Christchurch
       </a>
       in 1878 and Invercargill in 1879. Otago Boys' High School was founded in 1863. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago" title="University of Otago">
        University of Otago
       </a>
       , the oldest university in New Zealand, in 1869.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorrell1969_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorrell1969-37">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Girls%27_High_School" title="Otago Girls' High School">
        Otago Girls' High School
       </a>
       was established in 1871. Between 1881 and 1957, Dunedin was home to
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_cable_tramway_system" title="Dunedin cable tramway system">
        cable trams
       </a>
       , being both one of the first and last such systems in the world. Early in the 1880s the inauguration of the frozen meat industry, with the first shipment leaving from
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       in 1882, saw the beginning of a later great national industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1951_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1951-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After ten years of gold rushes the economy slowed but
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Vogel" title="Julius Vogel">
        Julius Vogel
       </a>
       's immigration and development scheme brought thousands more especially to Dunedin and Otago before recession set in again in the 1880s. In these first and second times of prosperity many institutions and businesses were established, New Zealand's first daily newspaper,
       <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">
        art school
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">
        medical school
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Public_art" title="Public art">
        public art
       </a>
       gallery the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Public_Art_Gallery" title="Dunedin Public Art Gallery">
        Dunedin Public Art Gallery
       </a>
       among them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949_26-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLintock1949-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDonald1965_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDonald1965-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was also a remarkable architectural flowering producing many substantial and ornamental buildings.
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lawson_(architect)" title="Robert Lawson (architect)">
        R.A. Lawson
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Church,_Dunedin" title="First Church, Dunedin">
        First Church of Otago
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Knox_Church,_Dunedin" title="Knox Church, Dunedin">
        Knox Church
       </a>
       are notable examples, as are buildings by
       <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_Bury" title="Maxwell Bury">
        Maxwell Bury
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Petre" title="Francis Petre">
        F.W. Petre
       </a>
       . The other visual arts also flourished under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/W._M._Hodgkins" title="W. M. Hodgkins">
        W. M. Hodgkins
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city's landscape and burgeoning townscape were vividly portrayed by
       <a href="/wiki/George_O%27Brien_(painter)" title="George O'Brien (painter)">
        George O'Brien 1821–1888
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinsEntwisle1986_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinsEntwisle1986-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the mid-1890s the economy revived. Institutions such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Toit%C5%AB_Otago_Settlers_Museum" title="Toitū Otago Settlers Museum">
        Toitū Otago Settlers Museum
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Hocken_Collections" title="Hocken Collections">
        Hocken Collections
       </a>
       – the first of their kind in New Zealand – were founded. More notable buildings such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_Railway_Station" title="Dunedin Railway Station">
        Railway Station
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Olveston_(house)" title="Olveston (house)">
        Olveston
       </a>
       were erected. New energy in the visual arts represented by
       <a href="/wiki/G._P._Nerli" title="G. P. Nerli">
        G.P. Nerli
       </a>
       culminated in the career of
       <a href="/wiki/Frances_Hodgkins" title="Frances Hodgkins">
        Frances Hodgkins
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1954_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1954-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisle1984-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEntwisleDunnCollins1988_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEntwisleDunnCollins1988-42">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunn2005_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunn2005-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_era">
        Early modern era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early modern era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="137" data-file-width="727" height="53" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg/280px-Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg/420px-Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg/560px-Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Historic panorama of the Botanical Gardens,
         <abbr title="circa">
          c.
         </abbr>
         <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
          1900
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By 1900, Dunedin was no longer the country's biggest city. Influence and activity moved north to the other centres ("the drift north"), a trend which continued for much of the following century. Despite this, the university continued to expand, and a student quarter became established. At the same time people started to notice Dunedin's mellowing, the ageing of its grand old buildings, with writers like E.H. McCormick pointing out its atmospheric charm.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1959_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1959-44">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1930s and early 1940s a new generation of artists such as
       <a href="/wiki/Toss_Woollaston" title="Toss Woollaston">
        M.T. (Toss) Woollaston
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Doris_Lusk" title="Doris Lusk">
        Doris Lusk
       </a>
       , Anne Hamblett,
       <a href="/wiki/Colin_McCahon" title="Colin McCahon">
        Colin McCahon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Hayman" title="Patrick Hayman">
        Patrick Hayman
       </a>
       once again represented the best of the country's talent. The Second World War saw the dispersal of these painters, but not before McCahon had met a very youthful poet,
       <a href="/wiki/James_K._Baxter" title="James K. Baxter">
        James K. Baxter
       </a>
       , in a central city studio.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cenotaph,_Dunedin,_New_Zealand2.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG/170px-Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG/255px-Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG/340px-Cenotaph%2C_Dunedin%2C_New_Zealand2.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cenotaph,_Dunedin,_New_Zealand2.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Cenotaph" title="Dunedin Cenotaph">
          Dunedin Cenotaph
         </a>
         , erected in 1927
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Numerous large companies had been established in Dunedin, many of which became national leaders. Late among them was
       <a href="/wiki/Fletcher_Construction" title="Fletcher Construction">
        Fletcher Construction
       </a>
       , founded by Sir
       <a href="/wiki/James_Fletcher_(industrialist)" title="James Fletcher (industrialist)">
        James Fletcher
       </a>
       in the early 20th century.
       <a href="/wiki/Kempthorne_Prosser" title="Kempthorne Prosser">
        Kempthorne Prosser
       </a>
       , established in 1879 in Stafford Street, was the largest fertiliser and drug manufacturer in the country for over 100 years.
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Methven_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Methven (company) (page does not exist)">
        G. Methven
       </a>
       , a metalworking and tap manufacturer based in
       <a href="/wiki/South_Dunedin" title="South Dunedin">
        South Dunedin
       </a>
       , was also a leading firm, as was
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ely_Shacklock" title="Henry Ely Shacklock">
        H. E. Shacklock
       </a>
       , an iron founder and appliance manufacturer later taken over by the Auckland concern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fisher_and_Paykel" title="Fisher and Paykel">
        Fisher and Paykel
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mosgiel_Woollens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mosgiel Woollens (page does not exist)">
        Mosgiel Woollens
       </a>
       was another Victorian Dunedin foundation.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hallensteins" title="Hallensteins">
        Hallensteins
       </a>
       was the colloquial name of a menswear manufacturer and national retail chain while the DIC and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthur_Barnett_(department_store)" title="Arthur Barnett (department store)">
        Arthur Barnett
       </a>
       were department stores, the former a nationwide concern. Coulls, Somerville Wilkie – later part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Whitcoulls" title="Whitcoulls">
        Whitcoulls
       </a>
       group – had its origins in Dunedin in the 19th century. There were also the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Mortgage_and_Agency_Company_of_New_Zealand" title="National Mortgage and Agency Company of New Zealand">
        National Mortgage and Agency Company of New Zealand
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wright_Stephenson" title="Wright Stephenson">
        Wright Stephensons Limited
       </a>
       , the Union Steamship Company and the National Insurance Company and the Standard Insurance Company among many others, which survived into the 20th century.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_developments">
        Post-war developments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-war developments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="993" data-file-width="3256" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg/280px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg/420px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg/560px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_winter_2011_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dunedin Botanic Gardens in winter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">
        Second World War
       </a>
       prosperity and population growth revived, although Dunedin trailed as the fourth 'main centre'. A generation reacting against
       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">
        Victorianism
       </a>
       started demolishing its buildings and many were lost, notably
       <a href="/wiki/William_Mason_(architect)" title="William Mason (architect)">
        William Mason
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">
        Stock exchange
       </a>
       in 1969. (
       <a href="/wiki/Princes_Street,_Dunedin" title="Princes Street, Dunedin">
        Dunedin Stock Exchange building
       </a>
       ) Although the university continued to expand, the city's population contracted, notably from 1976 to 1981. This was, however, a culturally vibrant time with the university's new privately endowed arts fellowships bringing such luminaries as
       <a href="/wiki/James_K._Baxter" title="James K. Baxter">
        James K Baxter
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hotere" title="Ralph Hotere">
        Ralph Hotere
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Janet_Frame" title="Janet Frame">
        Janet Frame
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hone_Tuwhare" title="Hone Tuwhare">
        Hone Tuwhare
       </a>
       to the city.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princes_Street,_Dunedin_1982_(35772469910).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="900" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg/220px-Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg/330px-Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg/440px-Princes_Street%2C_Dunedin_1982_%2835772469910%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princes_Street,_Dunedin_1982_(35772469910).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Princes Street in April 1982
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the 1980s Dunedin's
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">
        popular music
       </a>
       scene blossomed, with many acts, such as
       <a href="/wiki/The_Chills" title="The Chills">
        The Chills
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Clean" title="The Clean">
        The Clean
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Verlaines" title="The Verlaines">
        The Verlaines
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Straitjacket_Fits" title="Straitjacket Fits">
        Straitjacket Fits
       </a>
       , gaining national and international recognition. The term "The
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Sound" title="Dunedin Sound">
        Dunedin Sound
       </a>
       " was coined to describe the 1960s-influenced, guitar-led music which flourished at the time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bands and musicians are still playing and recording in many styles.
      </p>
      <p>
       By 1990,
       <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">
        population decline
       </a>
       had steadied and slow growth has occurred since and Dunedin re-invented itself as a 'heritage city' with its main streets refurbished in Victorian style.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heritage_buildings_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-heritage_buildings-46">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       R.A. Lawson's Municipal Chambers (
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Town_Hall" title="Dunedin Town Hall">
        Dunedin Town Hall
       </a>
       ) in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Octagon,_Dunedin" title="The Octagon, Dunedin">
        the Octagon
       </a>
       were handsomely restored. The city was also recognised as a centre of excellence in tertiary education and research. The university's and polytechnic's growth accelerated. Dunedin has continued to refurbish itself, embarking on redevelopments of the
       <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">
        art gallery
       </a>
       , railway station and the
       <a href="/wiki/Toit%C5%AB_Otago_Settlers_Museum" title="Toitū Otago Settlers Museum">
        Toitū Otago Settlers Museum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin has flourishing niche industries including engineering, software engineering,
       <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
        bio-technology
       </a>
       and fashion.
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       provides Dunedin with deep-water facilities. It is served by the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers_Branch" title="Port Chalmers Branch">
        Port Chalmers Branch
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Branch_line" title="Branch line">
        branch line
       </a>
       railway which diverges from the
       <a href="/wiki/Main_South_Line" title="Main South Line">
        Main South Line
       </a>
       and runs from
       <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
        Christchurch
       </a>
       by way of Dunedin to
       <a href="/wiki/Invercargill" title="Invercargill">
        Invercargill
       </a>
       . Dunedin is also home to
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MTF_Ltd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MTF Ltd (page does not exist)">
        MTF
       </a>
       , the nationwide vehicle finance company.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cityscape glitters with gems of Victorian and Edwardian architecture – the legacy of the city's gold-rush affluence. Many, including First Church,
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Boys%27_High_School" title="Otago Boys' High School">
        Otago Boys' High School
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Larnach_Castle" title="Larnach Castle">
        Larnach Castle
       </a>
       were designed by one of New Zealand's most eminent architects
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lawson_(architect)" title="Robert Lawson (architect)">
        R A Lawson
       </a>
       . Other prominent buildings include
       <a href="/wiki/Olveston_(house)" title="Olveston (house)">
        Olveston
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_Railway_Station" title="Dunedin Railway Station">
        Dunedin Railway Station
       </a>
       . Other unusual or memorable buildings or constructions are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baldwin_Street,_Dunedin" title="Baldwin Street, Dunedin">
        Baldwin Street
       </a>
       , claimed to be the world's steepest residential street;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Captain Cook tavern; Cadbury Chocolate Factory (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cadbury_World,_Dunedin" title="Cadbury World, Dunedin">
        Cadbury World
       </a>
       ); and the local
       <a href="/wiki/Speight%27s" title="Speight's">
        Speight's
       </a>
       brewery.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg/170px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg/255px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg/340px-Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Botanic_Gardens_Spring_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Botanic Gardens in Spring
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin is also a centre for
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       . The world's only mainland
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_royal_albatross" title="Northern royal albatross">
        royal albatross
       </a>
       colony and several penguin and
       <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">
        seal
       </a>
       colonies lie within the city boundaries on the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       . To the south, on the western side of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Waihola" title="Lake Waihola">
        Lake Waihola
       </a>
       , are the
       <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Wetlands" title="Sinclair Wetlands">
        Sinclair Wetlands
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The thriving tertiary student population has led to a vibrant
       <a href="/wiki/Youth_culture" title="Youth culture">
        youth culture
       </a>
       (students are referred to as 'Scarfies' by people who are not students), consisting of the previously mentioned
       <a href="/wiki/Indie_music_scene" title="Indie music scene">
        music scene
       </a>
       , and more recently a burgeoning boutique fashion industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thread_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-thread-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fashionherald_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fashionherald-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A strong visual arts community also exists in Dunedin, notably in
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       and the other settlements which dot the coast of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       , and also in communities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Waitati" title="Waitati">
        Waitati
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Sport is catered for in Dunedin by the floodlit
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" title="Rugby Union">
        rugby
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">
        cricket
       </a>
       venues of
       <a href="/wiki/Forsyth_Barr_Stadium" title="Forsyth Barr Stadium">
        Forsyth Barr Stadium
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_Oval,_Dunedin" title="University Oval, Dunedin">
        University Oval, Dunedin
       </a>
       respectively, the new
       <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_Ground" title="Caledonian Ground">
        Caledonian Ground
       </a>
       football and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" title="Track and field athletics">
        athletics
       </a>
       stadium near the University at
       <a href="/wiki/Logan_Park,_Dunedin" title="Logan Park, Dunedin">
        Logan Park
       </a>
       , the large
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Edgar_Centre" title="The Edgar Centre">
        Edgar Centre
       </a>
       indoor sports centre, the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Ice_Stadium" title="Dunedin Ice Stadium">
        Dunedin Ice Stadium
       </a>
       , and numerous golf courses and parks. There are also the
       <a href="/wiki/Forbury_Park_Raceway" title="Forbury Park Raceway">
        Forbury Park
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">
        horseracing
       </a>
       circuit in the south of the city and several others within a few kilometres. St Clair Beach is a well-known
       <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">
        surfing
       </a>
       venue, and the harbour basin is popular with
       <a href="/wiki/Windsurfing" title="Windsurfing">
        windsurfers
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" title="Kitesurfing">
        kitesurfers
       </a>
       . Dunedin has four public swimming pools:
       <a href="/wiki/Moana_Pool" title="Moana Pool">
        Moana Pool
       </a>
       , Port Chalmers Pool, Mosgiel, and St Clair Salt Water Pool.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3900" data-file-width="2613" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg/170px-Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg/255px-Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg/340px-Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taiaroa_Head_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Taiaroa_Head" title="Taiaroa Head">
          Taiaroa Head
         </a>
         with lighthouse.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin City has a land area of 3,314.8 square kilometres (1,279.9 sq mi), slightly larger than the American state of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">
        Rhode Island
       </a>
       or the English county of
       <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">
        Cambridgeshire
       </a>
       , and a little smaller than
       <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">
        Cornwall
       </a>
       . It was the largest city in land area in New Zealand until the formation of the 5,600 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (2,200 sq mi)
       <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Council" title="Auckland Council">
        Auckland Council
       </a>
       on 1 November 2010. The Dunedin City Council boundaries since 1989 have extended to
       <a href="/wiki/Middlemarch,_New_Zealand" title="Middlemarch, New Zealand">
        Middlemarch
       </a>
       in the west,
       <a href="/wiki/Waikouaiti" title="Waikouaiti">
        Waikouaiti
       </a>
       in the north, the Pacific Ocean in the east and south-east, and the Waipori/Taieri River and the township of
       <a href="/wiki/Henley,_New_Zealand" title="Henley, New Zealand">
        Henley
       </a>
       in the south-west.
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin is the farthest city in the world from London, the former Imperial capital, at 19,100 km (11,870 mi) (90 km (56 mi) more than
       <a href="/wiki/Invercargill" title="Invercargill">
        Invercargill
       </a>
       , and 100 km (62 mi) more than
       <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
        Christchurch
       </a>
       ), and from
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
        Berlin
       </a>
       at 18,200 km (11,310 mi). Its
       <a href="/wiki/Antipodes" title="Antipodes">
        antipodes
       </a>
       are some 300 km (190 mi) north of the Spanish city of
       <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">
        A Coruña
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin is situated at the head of
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       , a narrow inlet extending south-westward for some 15 miles. The harbour is a recent creation formed by the flooding of two river valleys.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the time of its foundation in 1848, the city has spread slowly over the low-lying
       <a href="/wiki/Flat_(landform)" title="Flat (landform)">
        flats
       </a>
       and nearby hills and across the
       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">
        isthmus
       </a>
       to the slopes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div aria-labelledby="Neighbouring_cities,_towns_and_places" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="padding:3px">
       <table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">

           </b>
          </div>
         </th>
        </tr>

          <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
           <table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin:0; text-align:center;">

              <a href="/wiki/Ranfurly,_New_Zealand" title="Ranfurly, New Zealand">

              </a>
              and
              <a href="/wiki/Alexandra,_New_Zealand" title="Alexandra, New Zealand">
               Alexandra
              </a>
             </td>

              <a href="/wiki/Oamaru" title="Oamaru">

              </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Inner_city">
        Inner city
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Inner city">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PrincesStDunedin.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="850" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/PrincesStDunedin.jpg/220px-PrincesStDunedin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/PrincesStDunedin.jpg/330px-PrincesStDunedin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/PrincesStDunedin.jpg/440px-PrincesStDunedin.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PrincesStDunedin.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Princes_Street" title="Princes Street">
          Princes Street
         </a>
         was developed during Dunedin's 1860s boom from the gold rush, and consequently is one of New Zealand's most historic streets.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The central region of Dunedin is known as
       <a href="/wiki/The_Octagon,_Dunedin" title="The Octagon, Dunedin">
        the Octagon
       </a>
       . It was once a gully, filled in the mid nineteenth century to create the present plaza. The initial settlement of the city took place to the south on the other side of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bell_Hill,_New_Zealand" title="Bell Hill, New Zealand">
        Bell Hill
       </a>
       , a large outcrop which had to be reduced to provide easy access between the two parts of the settlement. The central city stretches away from this point in a largely northeast-southwest direction, with the main streets of
       <a href="/wiki/George_Street,_Dunedin" title="George Street, Dunedin">
        George Street
       </a>
       and Princes Street meeting at The Octagon. Here they are joined by
       <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Street,_Dunedin" title="Stuart Street, Dunedin">
        Stuart Street
       </a>
       , which runs orthogonally to them, from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_Railway_Station" title="Dunedin Railway Station">
        Dunedin Railway Station
       </a>
       in the southeast, and steeply up to the suburb of Roslyn in the northwest. Many of the city's notable old buildings are located in the southern part of this area and on the inner ring of lower hills which surround the central city (most of these hills, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Maori_Hill" title="Maori Hill">
        Maori Hill
       </a>
       , Pine Hill, and Maryhill, rise to some 200 metres (660 ft) above the plain). The head of the harbour includes a large area of reclaimed land ("The Southern Endowment"), much of which is used for light industry and warehousing. A large area of flat land, simply known colloquially as "The Flat" lies to the south and southwest of the city centre, and includes several larger and older suburbs, notably
       <a href="/wiki/South_Dunedin" title="South Dunedin">
        South Dunedin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_New_Zealand" title="St Kilda, New Zealand">
        St. Kilda
       </a>
       . These are protected from the Pacific Ocean by a long line of dunes which run east-west along the city's southern coastline and separate residential areas from
       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Beach,_Otago" title="Ocean Beach, Otago">
        Ocean Beach
       </a>
       , which is traditionally divided into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Clair_Beach" title="St. Clair Beach">
        St. Clair Beach
       </a>
       at the western end and
       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Beach,_Otago" title="Ocean Beach, Otago">
        St. Kilda Beach
       </a>
       to the east.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG/220px-Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG/330px-Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG/440px-Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_from_Lookout.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dunedin seen from Unity Park lookout in the suburb of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mornington,_Otago" title="Mornington, Otago">
          Mornington
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="611" data-file-width="792" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg/220px-BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg/330px-BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg/440px-BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BaldwinStreet_Descending_Tourist.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_Street" title="Baldwin Street">
          Baldwin Street
         </a>
         in North East Valley is one of the world's steepest residential streets
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin is home to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baldwin_Street,_Dunedin" title="Baldwin Street, Dunedin">
        Baldwin Street
       </a>
       , which, according to the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">
         Guinness Book of Records
        </a>
       </i>
       , is the steepest street in the world. Its gradient is 1 in 2.9.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The long since abandoned Maryhill
       <a href="/wiki/Cable_car_(railway)" title="Cable car (railway)">
        Cablecar
       </a>
       route had a similar gradient close to its Mornington depot.
      </p>
      <p>
       Beyond the inner range of hills lie Dunedin's outer suburbs, notably to the northwest, beyond Roslyn. This direction contains Taieri Road and Three Mile Hill, which between them formed the original road route to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taieri_Plains" title="Taieri Plains">
        Taieri Plains
       </a>
       . The modern
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_1" title="New Zealand State Highway 1">
        State Highway 1
       </a>
       follows a different route, passing through
       <a href="/wiki/Caversham,_New_Zealand" title="Caversham, New Zealand">
        Caversham
       </a>
       in the west and out past Saddle Hill. Lying between Saddle Hill and Caversham are the outer suburbs of
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Island,_New_Zealand" title="Green Island, New Zealand">
        Green Island and Abbotsford
       </a>
       . Between Green Island and Roslyn lies the steep-sided valley of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kaikorai_Stream" title="Kaikorai Stream">
        Kaikorai Stream
       </a>
       , which is today a residential and light industrial area. Suburban settlements – mostly regarded as separate townships – also lie along both edges of the Otago Harbour. Notable among these are
       <a href="/wiki/Portobello,_New_Zealand" title="Portobello, New Zealand">
        Portobello
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Macandrew_Bay" title="Macandrew Bay">
        Macandrew Bay
       </a>
       , on the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       coast, and
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       on the opposite side of the harbour. Port Chalmers provides Dunedin's main deep-water port, including the city's container port.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dunedin skyline is dominated by a ring of (traditionally seven) hills which form the remnants of a
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_crater" title="Volcanic crater">
        volcanic crater
       </a>
       . Notable among them are
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cargill" title="Mount Cargill">
        Mount Cargill
       </a>
       (700 m (2,300 ft)),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagstaff,_Otago" title="Flagstaff, Otago">
        Flagstaff
       </a>
       (680 m (2,230 ft)),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saddle_Hill,_New_Zealand" title="Saddle Hill, New Zealand">
        Saddle Hill
       </a>
       (480 m (1,570 ft)),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Signal_Hill,_New_Zealand" title="Signal Hill, New Zealand">
        Signal Hill
       </a>
       (390 m (1,280 ft)), and Harbour Cone (320 m (1,050 ft)).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hinterland">
        Hinterland
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hinterland">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="800" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg/220px-Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg/330px-Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg/440px-Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_Otago_Peninsula_Harbour.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dunedin (grey area to lower left) sits close to the isthmus of the
         <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
          Otago Peninsula
         </a>
         , at the end of
         <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
          Otago Harbour
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin's hinterland encompasses a variety of different landforms. To the southwest lie the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taieri_Plains" title="Taieri Plains">
        Taieri Plains
       </a>
       , the broad, fertile lowland floodplains of the
       <a href="/wiki/Taieri_River" title="Taieri River">
        Taieri River
       </a>
       and its major tributary the
       <a href="/wiki/Waipori_River" title="Waipori River">
        Waipori
       </a>
       . These are moderately heavily settled, and contain the towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Mosgiel" title="Mosgiel">
        Mosgiel
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Allanton,_New_Zealand" title="Allanton, New Zealand">
        Allanton
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They are separated from the coast by a range of low hills rising to some 300 metres (980 ft). Inland from the Taieri Plain is rough hill country. Close to the plain, much of this is forested, notably around
       <a href="/wiki/Berwick,_New_Zealand" title="Berwick, New Zealand">
        Berwick
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mahinerangi" title="Lake Mahinerangi">
        Lake Mahinerangi
       </a>
       , and also around the
       <a href="/wiki/Silverpeaks" title="Silverpeaks">
        Silverpeaks
       </a>
       Range which lies northwest of the Dunedin urban area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBishopHamel1993_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBishopHamel1993-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Beyond this, the land becomes drier and opens out into grass and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tussock_grass" title="Tussock grass">
        tussock
       </a>
       -covered land. A high, broad valley, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strath-Taieri" title="Strath-Taieri">
        Strath-Taieri
       </a>
       lies in Dunedin's far northwest, containing the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Middlemarch,_New_Zealand" title="Middlemarch, New Zealand">
        Middlemarch
       </a>
       , one of the area's few concentrations of population.
      </p>
      <p>
       To the north of the city's urban area is undulating hill country containing several small, mainly coastal, settlements, including
       <a href="/wiki/Waitati" title="Waitati">
        Waitati
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Warrington,_New_Zealand" title="Warrington, New Zealand">
        Warrington
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Seacliff" title="Seacliff">
        Seacliff
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Waikouaiti" title="Waikouaiti">
        Waikouaiti
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_1" title="New Zealand State Highway 1">
        State Highway 1
       </a>
       winds steeply through a series of hills here, notably
       <a href="/wiki/The_Kilmog" title="The Kilmog">
        The Kilmog
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989_52-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These hills can be considered a coastal extension of the Silverpeaks Range.
      </p>
      <p>
       To the east, Dunedin City includes the entirety of the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Peninsula" title="Otago Peninsula">
        Otago Peninsula
       </a>
       , a long finger of land that formed the southeastern rim of the Dunedin Volcano.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989_52-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDannPeat1989-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The peninsula is lightly settled, almost entirely along the harbour coast, and much of it is maintained as a
       <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">
        natural habitat
       </a>
       by the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Otago_Peninsula_Trust&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Otago Peninsula Trust (page does not exist)">
        Otago Peninsula Trust
       </a>
       . The peninsula contains several fine beaches, and is home to a considerable number of
       <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">
        rare species
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow-eyed_penguin" title="Yellow-eyed penguin">
        yellow-eyed
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Little_penguin" title="Little penguin">
        little
       </a>
       penguins,
       <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">
        seals
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cormorant" title="Cormorant">
        shags
       </a>
       . Most importantly, it contains the world's only mainland breeding colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_royal_albatross" title="Southern royal albatross">
        royal albatross
       </a>
       , at
       <a href="/wiki/Taiaroa_Head" title="Taiaroa Head">
        Taiaroa Head
       </a>
       on the peninsula's northeastern point.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_suburbs">
        List of suburbs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: List of suburbs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Suburbs_of_Dunedin" title="Suburbs of Dunedin">
        Suburbs of Dunedin
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Clair,_New_Zealand.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/220px-St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/330px-St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/440px-St_Clair%2C_New_Zealand.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St_Clair,_New_Zealand.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Beach in the suburb of
         <a href="/wiki/St_Clair,_New_Zealand" title="St Clair, New Zealand">
          St Clair
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Inner suburbs
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
