      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The climate of Dunedin in general is temperate; however, the city is recognised as having a large number of microclimates and the weather conditions often vary between suburbs mostly due to the city's topographical layout.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       , Dunedin features an
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        oceanic climate
       </a>
       . The city's climate is also greatly modified by its proximity to the ocean. This leads to mild summers and cool winters. Winter is frosty but sunny, snowfall is common but significant snowfall is uncommon (perhaps every two or three years), except in the inland hill suburbs such as Halfway Bush and Wakari, which tend to receive a few days of snowfall each year. Spring can feature "four seasons in a day" weather, but from November to April it is generally settled and mild. Temperatures during summer can briefly reach 30 °C (86 °F). Due to its extreme maritime influence, Dunedin's cool summers and mild winters both stand out considering its latitude.
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin has relatively low rainfall in comparison to many of New Zealand's cities, with only some 750 millimetres (30 in) recorded per year. Despite this fact it is sometimes misguidedly regarded as a damp city,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       probably due to its rainfall occurring in drizzle or light rain (heavy rain is relatively rare). Dunedin is one of the cloudiest major centres in the country, recording approximately 1650 hours of bright sunshine per annum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prevailing_wind" title="Prevailing wind">
        Prevailing wind
       </a>
       in the city is mainly a sometimes cool southwesterly and during late spring will alternate with northeasterlies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Warmer, dry northwest winds are also characteristic
       <a href="/wiki/Nor%27west_arch" title="Nor'west arch">
        Foehn winds from the northwest
       </a>
       . The circle of hills surrounding the
       <a href="/wiki/Inner_city" title="Inner city">
        inner city
       </a>
       shelters the inner city from much of the prevailing weather, while hills just to the west of the city can often push inclement weather around to the west of the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       Inland, beyond the heart of the city and into inland Otago the climate is sub-continental: winters are quite cold and dry, summers hot and dry. Thick freezing ground fogs are common in winter in the upper reaches of the
       <a href="/wiki/Taieri_River" title="Taieri River">
        Taieri River
       </a>
       's course around
       <a href="/wiki/Middlemarch,_New_Zealand" title="Middlemarch, New Zealand">
        Middlemarch
       </a>
       , and in summer the temperature occasionally reaches 30 °C (86 °F).
      </p>

      <p>
       The city has a population of 128,800 (June 2017).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZ_population_data_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NZ_population_data-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Compared to New Zealand as a whole, Dunedin's demographics tend to show traits of the New Zealand education sector, largely caused by the city's high tertiary student population. These traits include a higher female population compared to males, a lower-than-average median age, a high proportion of people under 25 years, a higher proportion of people of European and Asian ethnicity and a lower proportion of Maori and Pacific Island ethnicities, higher unemployment, lower median income, and a higher proportion of those with school and post-school qualifications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the 2013 census, Dunedin City had a residential population of 120,249, an increase of 1,566, or 1.3 percent, since the 2006 census. There were 46,590 occupied dwellings, 3,915 unoccupied dwellings, and 186 dwellings under construction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Of the residential population, 56,931 (48.0%) were male compared to 48.8% nationally, and 61,752 (52.0%) were female, compared to 51.2% nationally. The city had a median age of 36.7 years, 1.3 years below the national median age of 38.0 years. People aged 65 and over made up 14.9% of the population, compared to 14.3% nationally, and people under 15 years made up 16.2%, compared to 20.4% nationally. Due to the large tertiary education sector, people aged between 15 and 24 made up approximately 21.6% of the city's residential population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin's ethnicity is made up of (national figures in brackets): 88.3% European (74.0%), 7.7% Maori (14.9%), 6.2% Asian (11.8%), 2.5% Pacific Islanders (7.4%), 1.0% Middle Eastern/Latin American/African (1.2%), and 2.1% 'New Zealanders' (1.6%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin had an unemployment rate of 7.5% of people 15 years and over, compared to 7.1% nationally. The median annual income of all people 15 years and over was $23,300, compared to 28,500 nationally. Of those, 44.8% earned under $20,000, compared to 43.2% nationally, while 22.0% earned over $50,000, compared to 26.7% nationally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_18-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In December 2014 Dunedin was designated as a
       <a href="/wiki/City_of_Literature" title="City of Literature">
        UNESCO Creative City of Literature
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mayor of Dunedin Dave Cull said at the time "This announcement puts our city on the world map as a first-class literary city. We keep honourable company; other cities bestowed with City of Literature status include Edinburgh, Dublin, Iowa City, Melbourne, Reykjavík, Norwich and Kraków."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin's application was driven by a steering committee and an advisory board of writers, librarians and academics from a range of Dunedin institutions. The bid highlighted the quality of the city's considerable literary heritage, its diverse combination of literary events, businesses, institutions and organisations, plus its thriving community of writers, playwrights and lyricists.
      </p>
      <p>
       UNESCO established the Creative Cities Network to develop international co-operation among cities and encourage them to drive joint development partnerships in line with UNESCO's global priorities of 'culture and development' and 'sustainable development'. Each city in the network reflects one of UNESCO's seven Creative City themes: folk art, gastronomy, literature, design, film or music. Dunedin is New Zealand’s first city to be appointed to the Creative City network.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Choirs">
        Choirs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Choirs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Dunedin is home to many choirs. These include the following:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The 140-member
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_of_Dunedin_Choir" title="City of Dunedin Choir">
         City of Dunedin Choir
        </a>
        is Dunedin's leading performer of large-scale choral works.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Southern_Consort_of_Voices" title="Southern Consort of Voices">
         Southern Consort of Voices
        </a>
        is a smaller choir regularly performing Choral Works.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dunedin_Male_Choir" title="Royal Dunedin Male Choir">
         Royal Dunedin Male Choir
        </a>
        , conducted by Richard Madden, performs two concerts a year
       </li>
       <li>
        The Dunedin RSA Choir regularly performs concerts and has played an important and valued role in Dunedin City's commemorative celebrations of significant historical events. ANZAC, of course, is one such occasion, and the ANZAC Revue held on the evening of every ANZAC Day, occupies a special place of honour in the choir's calendar.
       </li>
       <li>
        The all-female Dunedin Harmony Chorus are an important part of the Dunedin culture.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Southern Children's Choir, based in Marama Hall in the university, is Dunedin's main children's choir. Most schools in Dunedin have choirs, many having more than one.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Southern Youth Choir is a concert-based youth choir.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago" title="University of Otago">
         University of Otago
        </a>
        is home to three official choirs: the two chapel choirs (Knox and Selwyn), and the travelling
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cantores&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cantores (page does not exist)">
         Cantores
        </a>
        choir.
       </li>
       <li>
        Several Dunedin Churches and Cathedrals hold choirs. Among these are
        <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_Cathedral,_Dunedin" title="St. Joseph's Cathedral, Dunedin">
         St. Joseph's Catholic Cathedral
        </a>
        , home to two choirs: the Cathedral Choir and the Gabrieli Singers;
        <a href="/wiki/Knox_Church,_Dunedin" title="Knox Church, Dunedin">
         Knox Church
        </a>
        's large mixed gender choir for adults and children, the Knox Church Choir;
        <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Church,_Dunedin" title="All Saints' Church, Dunedin">
         All Saints' Church, Dunedin
        </a>
        , has choral scholars from
        <a href="/wiki/Selwyn_College,_Otago" title="Selwyn College, Otago">
         Selwyn College, Otago
        </a>
        , St. John's Church, Roslyn's small mixed-gender parish choir; and
        <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Cathedral,_Dunedin" title="St. Paul's Cathedral, Dunedin">
         St. Paul's Anglican Cathedral
        </a>
        's mixed-gender adult choir.
       </li>
       <li>
        The Dunedin
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">
         Red Cross
        </a>
        Choir (of New Zealand Red Cross), conducted by Eleanor Moyle, is one of only three Red Cross choirs globally. Established in 1942, this choir performs regularly in Dunedin at various Rest Homes and holds an annual concert at the Kings and Queens Performing Arts Centre.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Instrumental_classical_and_jazz_ensembles">
        Instrumental classical and jazz ensembles
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Instrumental classical and jazz ensembles">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Southern Sinfonia is a semi-professional orchestra based in Dunedin. Other instrumental ensembles include the Rare Byrds early music ensemble, the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Collegiate_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Collegiate Orchestra (page does not exist)">
        Collegiate Orchestra
       </a>
       , and the Dunedin Youth Orchestra. Many schools also hold school orchestras and bands. There are also three brass bands in Dunedin: St. Kilda Brass, Kaikorai Brass, and Mosgiel Brass. The Otago Symphonic Band and City of Dunedin Pipe Band are also important Dunedin musical ensembles.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_music">
        Popular music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Popular music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Dunedin lends its name to the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Sound" title="Dunedin Sound">
        Dunedin Sound
       </a>
       , a form of
       <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">
        indie
       </a>
       rock music which was created in the city in the 1980s. At that time, Dunedin was a fertile ground for bands, many of whom recorded on the
       <a href="/wiki/Flying_Nun_Records" title="Flying Nun Records">
        Flying Nun Records
       </a>
       label, based in Christchurch. Among the bands with strong Dunedin connections at this time were
       <a href="/wiki/The_Chills" title="The Chills">
        The Chills
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Clean" title="The Clean">
        The Clean
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Verlaines" title="The Verlaines">
        The Verlaines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Bats_(New_Zealand_band)" title="The Bats (New Zealand band)">
        The Bats
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sneaky_Feelings" title="Sneaky Feelings">
        Sneaky Feelings
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Dead_C" title="The Dead C">
        The Dead C
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Straitjacket_Fits" title="Straitjacket Fits">
        Straitjacket Fits
       </a>
       , all of which had significant followings throughout New Zealand and on the college radio circuit in the United States and Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin has also been home to a number of successful bands since the end of the Dunedin Sound era.
       <a href="/wiki/Six60" title="Six60">
        Six60
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Julian_Temple_Band" title="Julian Temple Band">
        Julian Temple Band
       </a>
       , Two Cartoons, Males, Summer Thieves and Albion Place are all good examples of Dunedin bands to have received national and international acclaim in recent years.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">
        Theatre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Theatre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FortunetheatreNZ.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="676" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/FortunetheatreNZ.jpg/220px-FortunetheatreNZ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/FortunetheatreNZ.jpg/330px-FortunetheatreNZ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/FortunetheatreNZ.jpg/440px-FortunetheatreNZ.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FortunetheatreNZ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Fortune Theatre, Dunedin">
          Fortune Theatre
         </a>
         lays claim to being the world's southernmost professional theatre company
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dunedin hosts the world's southernmost professional theatre company: The
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Fortune Theatre, Dunedin">
        Fortune Theatre
       </a>
       , as well as having a large theatre venue, the
       <a href="/wiki/Regent_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Regent Theatre, Dunedin">
        Regent Theatre
       </a>
       in the Octagon. Smaller theatres in Dunedin include the
       <a href="/wiki/Globe_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Globe Theatre, Dunedin">
        Globe Theatre
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mayfair_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Mayfair Theatre, Dunedin">
        Mayfair Theatre
       </a>
       , and the Playhouse Theatre.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">
        Visual arts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Visual arts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Dunedin has a substantial public art gallery, the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Public_Art_Gallery" title="Dunedin Public Art Gallery">
        Dunedin Public Art Gallery
       </a>
       , in the Octagon. The city contains numerous other galleries, including over a dozen dealer galleries, many of which are found south of the Octagon along
       <a href="/wiki/Princes_Street,_Dunedin" title="Princes Street, Dunedin">
        Princes Street
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moray_Place,_Dunedin" title="Moray Place, Dunedin">
        Moray Place
       </a>
       and Dowling Street. There are also several more experimental art spaces, notably the Blue Oyster Gallery in Dowling Street.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many notable artists have strong links with Dunedin, among them
       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hotere" title="Ralph Hotere">
        Ralph Hotere
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Frances_Hodgkins" title="Frances Hodgkins">
        Frances Hodgkins
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grahame_Sydney" title="Grahame Sydney">
        Grahame Sydney
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Harris_(artist)" title="Jeffrey Harris (artist)">
        Jeffrey Harris
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall,_Dunedin,_NZ.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3075" data-file-width="4100" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/220px-Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/330px-Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/440px-Town_Hall%2C_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>

          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall,_Dunedin,_NZ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Dunedin Town Hall
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Local">
        Local
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Local">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_City_Council" title="Dunedin City Council">
        Dunedin City Council
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1094" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg/170px-Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg/255px-Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg/340px-Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dave_Cull-Blueskin_News.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Dave_Cull" title="Dave Cull">
          Dave Cull
         </a>
         , current
         <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Dunedin" title="Mayor of Dunedin">
          Mayor of Dunedin
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Dunedin City Council (DCC) governs the Dunedin City territorial authority. It is made up of an elected mayor and 14 additional councillors elected across three wards, one of whom gets chosen as deputy mayor. The current
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Dunedin" title="Mayor of Dunedin">
        mayor
       </a>
       , first elected in the
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_mayoral_election,_2010" title="Dunedin mayoral election, 2010">
        2010 mayoral election
       </a>
       , is
       <a href="/wiki/Dave_Cull" title="Dave Cull">
        Dave Cull
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms_and_flag">
        Coat of arms and flag
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Coat of arms and flag">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The city's
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">
        coat of arms
       </a>
       , which were granted in 1947
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">
        Lord Lyon King of Arms
       </a>
       , are
       <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">
        emblazoned
       </a>
       as:
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">
         Argent
        </a>
        above a
        <a href="/wiki/Fess" title="Fess">
         Fess
        </a>
        Dancette Vert, a Castle Triple-Towered
        <a href="/wiki/Sable_(heraldry)" title="Sable (heraldry)">
         sable
        </a>
        on a Rock issuing from the Fess, Masoned
        <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">
         Argent
        </a>
        , with Windows, Vanes and Portcullis
        <a href="/wiki/Gules" title="Gules">
         Gules
        </a>
        . In the base a Three-Masted Lymphad with Sail Furled Azure, Flagged of
        <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
         Scotland
        </a>
        , a Ram's Head Affrontee Horned
        <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">
         Or
        </a>
        between Two Garbs of the last
       </i>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supporters" title="Supporters">
        supporters
       </a>
       are blazoned as:
       <i>
        On the
        <a href="/wiki/Dexter_and_sinister" title="Dexter and sinister">
         Dexter
        </a>
        a Scotsman Habited with Philabeg and Plaid of the
        <a href="/wiki/Clan_Cameron" title="Clan Cameron">
         Clan Cameron
        </a>
        , supporting in His Exterior Hand a Cromach; on the
        <a href="/wiki/Dexter_and_sinister" title="Dexter and sinister">
         Sinister
        </a>
        a Maori Chief attired in
        <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_traditional_textiles#Korowai" title="Māori traditional textiles">
         Korowai
        </a>
        , Two
        <a href="/wiki/Huia" title="Huia">
         Huia
        </a>
        Feathers in his hair, an Aurei and a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hei_Matau" title="Hei Matau">
         Hei Matau
        </a>
        and in His Exterior hand a
        <a href="/wiki/Taiaha" title="Taiaha">
         Taiaha
        </a>
        . All Proper.
       </i>
      </p>
      <p>
       The castle is taken from the
       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Edinburgh" title="Coat of arms of Edinburgh">
        arms of Edinburgh
       </a>
       , while the green fess and garb/animals signify regional agriculture and crops. At the base, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lymphad" title="Lymphad">
        lymphad
       </a>
       , or ship, alludes to the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
        Scottish
       </a>
       immigrants to the Otago region. The supporters reperesent the original Maori owners of the land and its Scottish purchasers. All of the elements of the arms are crowned with a
       <a href="/wiki/Mural_crown" title="Mural crown">
        mural crown
       </a>
       , emblematic of local government. Their motto is:
       <i>
        Maiorum Institutis Utendo
       </i>
       , or in
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        By following in the steps of our forefathers
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The flag of the city of Dunedin is a
       <a href="/wiki/Banner_of_arms" title="Banner of arms">
        banner of arms
       </a>
       in white and green and featuring the castle, lymphad, ram's head and wheat sheafs as on the coat of arms.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National">
        National
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: National">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Dunedin is covered by two general electorates:
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_North_(New_Zealand_electorate)" title="Dunedin North (New Zealand electorate)">
        Dunedin North
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_South" title="Dunedin South">
        Dunedin South
       </a>
       , and one
       <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_electorates" title="Māori electorates">
        Māori electorate
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Te_Tai_Tonga" title="Te Tai Tonga">
        Te Tai Tonga
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city in general is a stronghold of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Labour_Party" title="New Zealand Labour Party">
        New Zealand Labour Party
       </a>
       , having won the Dunedin-based electorate seats continuously since the 1978 election. As of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_general_election,_2017" title="New Zealand general election, 2017">
        2017 general election
       </a>
       , both general electorates are held by the party, with
       <a href="/wiki/David_Clark_(New_Zealand_politician)" title="David Clark (New Zealand politician)">
        David Clark
       </a>
       representing Dunedin North and
       <a href="/wiki/Clare_Curran" title="Clare Curran">
        Clare Curran
       </a>
       representing Dunedin South. Te Tai Tonga (which covers the entire South Island and part of
       <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">
        Wellington
       </a>
       in the North Island) is currently also held by the Labour Party and represented by
       <a href="/wiki/Rino_Tirikatene" title="Rino Tirikatene">
        Rino Tirikatene
       </a>
       . In addition to electorate MPs,
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Woodhouse" title="Michael Woodhouse">
        Michael Woodhouse
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_National_Party" title="New Zealand National Party">
        National Party
       </a>
       is a Dunedin-based list MP.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The major daily newspaper is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Otago_Daily_Times" title="Otago Daily Times">
         Otago Daily Times
        </a>
       </i>
       , which is also the country's oldest daily newspaper and part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Allied_Press" title="Allied Press">
        Allied Press
       </a>
       group. Weekly and bi-weekly community newspapers include
       <i>
        The Star
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Taieri_Herald&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Taieri Herald (page does not exist)">
         Taieri Herald
        </a>
       </i>
       , the fortnightly street press
       <i>
        POINT
       </i>
       , and student magazines
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Critic_(magazine)" title="Critic (magazine)">
         Critic
        </a>
       </i>
       (University of Otago) and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gyro_(magazine)" title="Gyro (magazine)">
         Gyro
        </a>
       </i>
       (Otago Polytechnic).
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is served by all major national radio and television stations. The city's main terrestrial television and FM radio transmitter sits atop
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cargill" title="Mount Cargill">
        Mount Cargill
       </a>
       , north of the city, while the city's main AM transmitter is located at Highcliff, east of the city centre on the Otago Peninsula. Local radio stations include
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Dunedin" title="Radio Dunedin">
        Radio Dunedin
       </a>
       , community station
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otago_Access_Radio" title="Otago Access Radio">
        Otago Access Radio
       </a>
       (formerly Hills AM, then Toroa Radio), and the university radio station,
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_One_(New_Zealand)" title="Radio One (New Zealand)">
        Radio One
       </a>
       . The city has one local television station,
       <a href="/wiki/39_Dunedin_Television" title="39 Dunedin Television">
        Dunedin Television
       </a>
       , part of Allied Press.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is home to several prominent media-related production companies, notably
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_History_New_Zealand" title="Natural History New Zealand">
        Natural History New Zealand
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taylormade_Media" title="Taylormade Media">
        Taylormade Media
       </a>
       . Dunedin was the location of one of the four television broadcasting installations established in the sixties by the NZBC, operating under the name
       <a href="/wiki/DNTV2" title="DNTV2">
        DNTV2
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city was once home to the head offices of
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Otago" title="Radio Otago">
        Radio Otago
       </a>
       – now called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RadioWorks" title="RadioWorks">
        RadioWorks
       </a>
       (part of
       <a href="/wiki/MediaWorks_New_Zealand" title="MediaWorks New Zealand">
        Mediaworks
       </a>
       ) and based in Auckland. It was also formerly the home to several now-defunct newspapers, prominent among which were the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Otago_Witness" title="Otago Witness">
         Otago Witness
        </a>
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evening_Star_(Dunedin)" title="Evening Star (Dunedin)">
         Evening Star
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin,_NZ.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="686" data-file-width="1024" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/280px-University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/420px-University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg/560px-University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin%2C_NZ.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Otago_in_Dunedin,_NZ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_University_of_Otago" title="The University of Otago">
          The University of Otago
         </a>
         , considered one of the world's most beautiful universities.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
          <a href="#cite_note-61">
           [60]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
          <a href="#cite_note-62">
           [61]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otago_Boys_School,_Dunedin.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg/170px-Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg/255px-Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg/340px-Otago_Boys_School%2C_Dunedin.jpg 2x" width="170"/>

         </div>
         Otago Boys School
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_the_Otago_Region#Dunedin_City" title="List of schools in the Otago Region">
        List of schools in the Otago Region § Dunedin_City
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary">
        Secondary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Secondary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Dunedin is home to 12 secondary schools: eight state and four
       <a href="/wiki/State-integrated_school" title="State-integrated school">
        state-integrated
       </a>
       . The oldest secondary school is state-run
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Boys%27_High_School" title="Otago Boys' High School">
        Otago Boys' High School
       </a>
       , founded in 1863. Its sister school,
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Girls%27_High_School" title="Otago Girls' High School">
        Otago Girls' High School
       </a>
       (1871) is the oldest state girls' secondary school in New Zealand, even though it preceded the state education system by six years.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other state schools include
       <a href="/wiki/Bayfield_High_School,_Dunedin" title="Bayfield High School, Dunedin">
        Bayfield High School
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kaikorai_Valley_College" title="Kaikorai Valley College">
        Kaikorai Valley College
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Logan_Park_High_School" title="Logan Park High School">
        Logan Park High School
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/King%27s_High_School,_Dunedin" title="King's High School, Dunedin">
        King's High School
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_High_School,_Dunedin" title="Queen's High School, Dunedin">
        Queen's High School
       </a>
       are single-sex schools based in
       <a href="/wiki/St_Clair,_New_Zealand" title="St Clair, New Zealand">
        St Clair
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Taieri_College" title="Taieri College">
        Taieri College
       </a>
       in Mosgiel. The four state-integrated schools are
       <a href="/wiki/Columba_College" title="Columba College">
        Columba College
       </a>
       , a Presbyterian girls' school;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Hilda%27s_Collegiate_School" title="St. Hilda's Collegiate School">
        St. Hilda's Collegiate School
       </a>
       , an Anglican girls' school;
       <a href="/wiki/John_McGlashan_College" title="John McGlashan College">
        John McGlashan College
       </a>
       , a Presbyterian boys' school; and
       <a href="/wiki/Kavanagh_College" title="Kavanagh College">
        Kavanagh College
       </a>
       , a Catholic coeducational school.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary">
        Tertiary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tertiary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago" title="University of Otago">
         University of Otago
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago_College_of_Education" title="University of Otago College of Education">
           Dunedin College of Education
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Otago_Polytechnic" title="Otago Polytechnic">
         Otago Polytechnic
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health_and_hospitals">
        Public health and hospitals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Public health and hospitals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Publicly funded primary health and hospital services are provided by the
       <a href="/wiki/District_health_board" title="District health board">
        Southern District Health Board
       </a>
       (Southern DHB).
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Public_Hospital" title="Dunedin Public Hospital">
        Dunedin Public Hospital
       </a>
       is the main public hospital in Dunedin. Other hospitals include the Mercy Hospital and the
       <a href="/wiki/Wakari_Hospital" title="Wakari Hospital">
        Wakari Hospital
       </a>
       . The Dunedin Public Hospital and the Wakari Hospital, which are closely related, are operated by Southern DHB.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ambulance services are provided by
       <a href="/wiki/St_John_New_Zealand" title="St John New Zealand">
        St John New Zealand
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Dunedin" title="Public transport in Dunedin">
        Public transport in Dunedin
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Road">
        Road
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Road">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Dunedin urban area is served by two
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_state_highway_network" title="New Zealand state highway network">
        state highways
       </a>
       , with an additional two state highways and one tourist route serving other parts of the district. The main state highway in Dunedin is
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_1" title="New Zealand State Highway 1">
        State Highway 1
       </a>
       , which runs in a north to south-west direction through the middle of the city, connecting Dunedin with Invercargill to the south and Timaru and Christchurch to the north. Between The Oval and Mosgiel, State Highway 1 follows the eleven-kilometre
       <a href="/wiki/Dunedin_Southern_Motorway" title="Dunedin Southern Motorway">
        Dunedin Southern Motorway
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_88" title="New Zealand State Highway 88">
        State Highway 88
       </a>
       connects central Dunedin to the city's port facilities at
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other State Highways in the city are:
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_86" title="New Zealand State Highway 86">
        State Highway 86
       </a>
       connecting SH 1 at Allanton with Dunedin International Airport,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_87" title="New Zealand State Highway 87">
        State Highway 87
       </a>
       connecting SH 1 at Kinmont with
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_State_Highway_85" title="New Zealand State Highway 85">
        SH 85
       </a>
       at Kyeburn via Middlemarch, serving the Dunedin city hinterland.
      </p>
      <p>
       Dunedin is the northeastern terminus of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Scenic_Route" title="Southern Scenic Route">
        Southern Scenic Route
       </a>
       , a tourist highway connecting Dunedin to Te Anau via
       <a href="/wiki/The_Catlins" title="The Catlins">
        The Catlins
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Invercargill" title="Invercargill">
        Invercargill
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Fiordland" title="Fiordland">
        Fiordland
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Low_floor.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="1969" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Low_floor.jpg/220px-Low_floor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Low_floor.jpg/330px-Low_floor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Low_floor.jpg/440px-Low_floor.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Low_floor.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Three
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DesignLine_Corporation" title="DesignLine Corporation">
          Designline
         </a>
         -built buses, operated by Citibus (now Go Bus) on Dunedin urban routes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">
        Bus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Buses in Dunedin are organised by the Otago Regional Council. A total of 64 buses operate on 17 weekday routes and 13 weeknight/weekend/holiday routes across the city. Buses are run by two operators, Ritchies Transport with three routes and Go Bus Transport with the remainder. Dunedin City Council-owned operator
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citibus_(New_Zealand)" title="Citibus (New Zealand)">
        Citibus
       </a>
       was a major player until 2011 when Passenger Transport (New Zealand) purchased Citibus from Dunedin City Holdings, and both companies were subsequently bought by Go Bus.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_Railway_Station" title="Dunedin Railway Station">
        Dunedin Railway Station
       </a>
       , located east of the Octagon, is the city's main railway station. Once the nation's busiest, decline in rail over the years saw the withdrawal of most services. Suburban services ceased in 1982, and the last regular commercial passenger train to serve Dunedin,
       <a href="/wiki/Southerner_(New_Zealand_train)" title="Southerner (New Zealand train)">
        The Southerner
       </a>
       , was cancelled in February 2002. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taieri_Gorge_Railway" title="Taieri Gorge Railway">
        Taieri Gorge Railway
       </a>
       currently operates tourist-oriented services from the station, the most prominent of which is the Taieri Gorge Limited, a popular and famous train operated daily along the former
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Central_Railway" title="Otago Central Railway">
        Otago Central Railway
       </a>
       through the scenic
       <a href="/wiki/Taieri_Gorge" title="Taieri Gorge">
        Taieri Gorge
       </a>
       . Taieri Gorge Railway also operates to
       <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_New_Zealand" title="Palmerston, New Zealand">
        Palmerston
       </a>
       once weekly. The station is also sometimes visited by excursions organised by other
       <a href="/wiki/Heritage_railway" title="Heritage railway">
        heritage railway
       </a>
       societies, and by trains chartered by
       <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">
        cruise ships
       </a>
       docking at Port Chalmers.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="1424" height="66" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg/220px-Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg/330px-Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg/440px-Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunedin_International_Airport3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_International_Airport" title="Dunedin International Airport">
          Dunedin International Airport
         </a>
         – an Air New Zealand 737 lands on the runway while an Air New Zealand A320 waits on the taxiway
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunedin_International_Airport" title="Dunedin International Airport">
        Dunedin International Airport
       </a>
       is located 22 km (13.67 mi) southwest of the city, on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taieri_Plains" title="Taieri Plains">
        Taieri Plains
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Momona" title="Momona">
        Momona
       </a>
       . The airport operates a single terminal and 1,900-metre (6,200 ft) runway, and is the third-busiest airport in the South Island, after Christchurch and Queenstown. It is primarily used for domestic flights, with regular flights to and from
       <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">
        Auckland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
        Christchurch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">
        Wellington
       </a>
       and charter flights to and from
       <a href="/wiki/Queenstown,_New_Zealand" title="Queenstown, New Zealand">
        Queenstown
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wanaka" title="Wanaka">
        Wanaka
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Invercargill" title="Invercargill">
        Invercargill
       </a>
       , but it also has international flights arriving from and departing to
       <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">
        Brisbane
       </a>
       year round. In recent years, a decline in International passengers can be attributed to fewer international flights operating direct to the airport.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">
        Sea
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sea">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Ferries operated between
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Chalmers" title="Port Chalmers">
        Port Chalmers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portobello,_New_Zealand" title="Portobello, New Zealand">
        Portobello
       </a>
       in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Occasional calls have been made to revive them, and a non-profit organisation, Otago ferries Inc., has been set up to examine the logistics of restoring one of the original ferries and again using it for this route.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1866, plans were made for a bridge across the
       <a href="/wiki/Otago_Harbour" title="Otago Harbour">
        Otago Harbour
       </a>
       between Port Chalmers and Portobello,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayward199865_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayward199865-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but this grand scheme for an 1140-metre structure never eventuated. Plans were also mooted during the 1870s for a canal between the Pacific coast at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomahawk,_New_Zealand" title="Tomahawk, New Zealand">
        Tomahawk
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andersons_Bay" title="Andersons Bay">
        Andersons Bay
       </a>
       , close to the head of the harbour.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayward199866_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayward199866-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This scheme also never came to fruition.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_events">
        Annual events
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Annual events">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        January – Whare Flat Folk Festival ends
       </li>
       <li>
        February – New Zealand Masters Games (Biennial event)
       </li>
       <li>
        February – Otago University Students' Association &amp; Otago Polytechnic Orientation Weeks
       </li>
       <li>
        February – Dunedin Summer Festival
       </li>
       <li>
        February – Thieves' Alley Market Day
       </li>
       <li>
        March –
        <a href="/wiki/Fringe_theatre" title="Fringe theatre">
         Fringe Festival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        March/April –
        <a href="/wiki/ID_Dunedin_Fashion_Week" title="ID Dunedin Fashion Week">
         iD Dunedin Fashion Week
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        May –
        <a href="/wiki/Capping_week" title="Capping week">
         Capping week
        </a>
        (University of Otago) including the
        <a href="/wiki/Capping_Show" title="Capping Show">
         Capping Show
        </a>
        run by the
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.ousa.org.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Otago University Students' Association
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        May –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.otagorally.net/home" rel="nofollow">
         International Rally of Otago
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        May –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.dunedinwritersfestival.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Dunedin Writers &amp; Readers Festival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        May –
        <a href="/wiki/Regent_Theatre,_Dunedin" title="Regent Theatre, Dunedin">
         Regent Theatre 24-hour book sale
        </a>
        (reputedly the southern hemisphere's largest regularly held
        <a href="/wiki/Used_book" title="Used book">
         second-hand book
        </a>
        sale)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
         <a href="#cite_note-67">
          [66]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        June –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.midwintercarnival.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Dunedin Midwinter Carnival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        June – Polar Plunge
       </li>
       <li>
        July –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.ousa.org.nz/events/reorientation/" rel="nofollow">
         Reorientation
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        July – New Zealand International Science Festival (every second year)
       </li>
       <li>
        July – Taste Otago Dunedin Food and Wine Festival
       </li>
       <li>
        July –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.chocolatecarnival.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Cadbury Chocolate Carnival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        July –
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.enzedff.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Dunedin International Film Festival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        August–September –
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110610171826/http://www.otago.ac.nz/German/play/" rel="nofollow">
         The German play at Otago University
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        September –
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110420040124/http://www.moromarathon.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Moro Marathon
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        September –
        <a class="external text" href="http://dunedinbeerfest.co.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Dunedin Beer Festival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        October – Otago Festival of the Arts – every second year (even numbered years)
       </li>
       <li>
        October –
        <a href="/wiki/Rhododendron" title="Rhododendron">
         Rhododendron
        </a>
        Week
       </li>
       <li>
        December –
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100525112018/http://www.samstock.org.nz/" rel="nofollow">
         Samstock Music Festival
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        December –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Parade" title="Santa Parade">
         Santa Parade
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        December – Whare Flat Folk Festival begins
       </li>
       <li>
        December – New Year's Eve Party Octagon
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">
        Twin towns and sister cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dunedin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Dunedin is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">
        twinned
       </a>
       with several cities throughout the world. These include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
          <img alt="United Kingdom" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">
         Edinburgh
        </a>
        , Scotland,
        <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
         United Kingdom
        </a>
        (1974)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
         <a href="#cite_note-68">
          [67]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edinburgh_twinning_69-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Edinburgh_twinning-69">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
          <img alt="Japan" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otaru,_Hokkaid%C5%8D" title="Otaru, Hokkaidō">
         Otaru
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Shiribeshi_Subprefecture" title="Shiribeshi Subprefecture">
         Shiribeshi Subprefecture
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">
         Hokkaido
        </a>
        , Japan (1980)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
         <a href="#cite_note-70">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
          <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">
         Portsmouth
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">
         Virginia
        </a>
        , United States of America (1962)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
         <a href="#cite_note-71">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
          <img alt="China" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
         Shanghai
        </a>
        , China (1994)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
         <a href="#cite_note-72">
          [71]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

            <a href="#cite_ref-17">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The description of Auckland, Wellington, Christchurch and Dunedin as the four main centres neatly divides the country geographically into northern and southern halves of each of the two main islands. These centres are thus described in a wide range of fields, from encyclopedias of New Zealand
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
            <a href="#cite_note-10">
             [10]
            </a>
           </sup>
           to scientific research institutes,
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
            <a href="#cite_note-11">
             [11]
            </a>
           </sup>
           the tourism industry
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
            <a href="#cite_note-12">
             [12]
            </a>
           </sup>
           to nationwide organisations
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
            <a href="#cite_note-13">
             [13]
            </a>
           </sup>
           and government departments,
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
            <a href="#cite_note-14">
             [14]
            </a>
           </sup>
           and from the entertainment industry
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
            <a href="#cite_note-15">
             [15]
            </a>
           </sup>
           to newspaper reports.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">

             [16]

          </span>
